Setting: Sherry’s living room – NIGHT. The warm glow of the lamps casts long shadows, creating a cozy yet intimate atmosphere. The remnants of their earlier conversation linger in the air.

INT. LIVING ROOM – NIGHT

Scene: Processing the Moment 

Setting: Sherry’s bedroom, later that night. The room is dimly lit by a bedside lamp, casting soft shadows. The atmosphere is quiet and introspective.

INT. SHERRY’S BEDROOM – LATE NIGHT

(SOUND: The faint hum of the heater, the quiet ticking of a small clock on her nightstand, the distant, muffled sound of Jeff moving around in the living room.)

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): The camera focuses on Sherry’s face as she lies in bed, staring up at the ceiling. The soft light illuminates her features, revealing the mix of emotions playing across her face: confusion, disappointment, and a lingering trace of the earlier excitement. The camera then pulls back slightly, showing her wrapped in her blanket, her body curled into a fetal position.

(LISA RUBIN): “This visual should emphasize Sherry’s vulnerability and her internal struggle.”

SHERRY (V.O.) What was that?

Sherry exhales deeply, her brow furrowing slightly. She replays the events of the past few hours in her mind, trying to make sense of Jeff’s behavior.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A quick flashback montage of key moments from the previous scene: Jeff’s intense focus on his guitar, his oblivious responses to her attempts at connection, the look of awe on his face when he finally truly saw her, and then his immediate return to his music. These flashes are quick and impressionistic, conveying Sherry’s fragmented memories of the night.

SHERRY (V.O.) He looked at me… really looked at me. For a second.

SHERRY (V.O.) And then… nothing.

She sits up, hugging her knees to her chest. Her fingers absentmindedly trace the pattern on her blanket.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A close-up of Sherry’s fingers tracing the pattern on the blanket, a subtle visual representation of her nervous energy.

SHERRY (V.O.) He said I pulled things out of him. Moments. Ideas. But… did I pull anything out of him?

She leans back against the headboard, her gaze drifting to the window.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A shot of the moonlight filtering through the window, casting long shadows across the room.

SHERRY (V.O.) Maybe I’m expecting too much. He’s an artist. This is what they do, right? They disappear into their own world.

She shakes her head slightly, a flicker of defiance in her eyes.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A close-up of Sherry’s face, her expression now determined.

SHERRY (V.O.) But I’m not just some groupie. I’m not just a muse. I’m… here.

She reaches for her phone on the nightstand, hesitating for a moment before unlocking it. She scrolls through her contacts, finally stopping on her sister’s name.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A close-up of Sherry’s hand as she taps her sister’s name on her phone.

SISTER (V.O.) (murmuring sleepily) Sherry? Do you have any idea what time it is? 

SHERRY (quickly) I know, I know. I’m sorry. I just… I needed to talk to someone. 

Her sister sighs audibly, but her tone softens. 

SISTER (V.O.) What’s going on? 

Sherry hesitates, her fingers brushing over the edge of the blanket as she searches for the right words. 

SHERRY I think I’m falling for him. 

SISTER (V.O.) (flatly) Oh, Lord. 

SHERRY (defensive) Don’t start. 

SISTER (V.O.) I’m not starting. I’m just… worried. 

SHERRY (sincerely) Don’t be. It’s not like that. 

Her sister’s pause on the other end of the line speaks volumes. 

SISTER (V.O.) Sherry, I know you. When you care about someone, you go all in. That’s great for most people, but Jeff’s not most people. 

SHERRY (sharply) What’s that supposed to mean? 

SISTER (V.O.) It means he’s used to a different kind of life. A fast one. Messy. And you’re… you’re you. 

Sherry’s voice softens, but there’s an edge of frustration in it. 

SHERRY 

You don’t think I can handle it? 

SISTER (V.O.) (sincerely) I think you’re trying to handle it. But have you thought about what happens if it doesn’t work out? 

Sherry presses her lips together, her fingers tightening around the phone. 

SHERRY I can’t think like that. Not now. 

SISTER (V.O.) (sighing) I just want you to be careful. 

Sherry’s Optimism 

Sherry glances toward the door again, her expression softening. 

SHERRY (quietly) I don’t know. There’s something about him. Something real. 

Her sister’s voice grows gentler, though still tinged with caution. 

SISTER (V.O.) If it feels real to you, then it is. Just don’t lose yourself in him, okay? 

SHERRY (smiling faintly) I won’t. 

SISTER (V.O.) Promise? 

Sherry leans back, staring up at the ceiling. 

SHERRY (sincerely) I promise. 

After the Call 

Sherry ends the call and sets the phone on the nightstand. She lies back, staring at the Def Leppard poster for a long moment before turning onto her side. The faint sound of Jeff’s guitar strumming drifts through the house, and a small smile tugs at her lips. 

SHERRY (V.O.) He’s worth it. 

The camera lingers on her face, her expression a mix of hope, determination, and vulnerability. 





Scene: Strengthening the Bond

The table is neatly set with folded napkins, fresh orange juice, and an arrangement of plates. This visual establishes Sherry’s domesticity, her desire to create a welcoming environment, and her quirky personality.

Scene 10: Jeff’s Internal Responses (Revised and Extended)

(SOUND: The quiet sounds of late morning: the distant hum of traffic, the occasional bird call, and the almost inaudible ticking of a clock. A sense of quiet contemplation pervades the scene.)

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): Jeff sits on the couch, his guitar resting across his lap, his fingers lightly tracing the strings. The leather-bound journal Sherry gave him sits unopened on the coffee table, a stark contrast to his well-worn, heavily annotated notebook lying beside it. The room is bathed in the soft light of late morning.

JEFF (V.O.) She’s… something else. No fucking doubt about that. Smart. Funny. Doesn’t take my shit.

He pauses, his fingers hovering over the strings as his gaze drifts to the journal.

JEFF (V.O.) And she’s trying. Really trying. More than any woman I’ve… actually, more than anyone, period.

A faint smile tugs at his lips, but it quickly fades, replaced by a look of confusion and unease.

JEFF (V.O.) But what the hell am I supposed to do with that? I’m not exactly relationship material.

He sets the guitar aside, leaning forward to pick up the journal. He runs his thumb over the intricate design on the cover, a look of genuine appreciation in his eyes.

JEFF (V.O.) This is… beautiful. She really gets me. Or at least, she thinks she does.

He opens the journal, flipping through the blank pages.

JEFF (V.O.) She says she wants to be part of my world. But my world… it’s a goddamn mess. It’s music, it’s late nights, it’s self-doubt, it’s people wanting a piece of me I don’t even have to give. It’s not… pancakes and sunshine.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A quick, fragmented montage flashes through Jeff’s mind: images of crowded bars, flashing lights, adoring fans, demanding record executives, and then a quick cut to Sherry’s smiling face. The montage is fast-paced and disorienting, reflecting his internal chaos.

JEFF (V.O.) I can barely keep my own shit together half the time. How am I supposed to factor in someone else’s needs? Especially someone like her?

He closes the journal with a sigh, a look of frustration crossing his face.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): Jeff sets the journal back down and stands, stretching, his muscles stiff from sleeping on the couch. His gaze drifts toward the kitchen, where Sherry is tidying up. He watches her for a moment, his expression a mixture of admiration and bewilderment.

JEFF (V.O.) She seemed… happy this morning. Or at least, she was pretending to be. That’s good, right? That’s what women want, isn’t it? To be… happy?

He rubs the back of his neck, frowning slightly.

JEFF (V.O.) But there was something… underneath. Like she was waiting for something I wasn’t giving her. What the fuck was that about?

He shakes his head, muttering under his breath, a genuine note of frustration in his voice.

JEFF (Muttering) Women. I’ll never fucking understand them.

Sherry turns, catching his movement.

SHERRY Everything okay?

Jeff forces a smile, nodding.

JEFF Yeah, just… thinking about the song.

SHERRY (Smiling) Anything good?

Jeff chuckles, picking up his guitar again.

JEFF You’ll have to wait and see.


Jeff’s Attempt to Reassure Himself

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): He sits back down, plucking the melody of “Incognito Window Worship.” His mind continues to race, even as his outward demeanor remains calm.

JEFF (V.O.) She gets the music. That’s the important thing. That’s… rare. But maybe she’s expecting too much. Maybe this whole thing is a fucking mistake.

His fingers falter on the strings, and he leans back, exhaling sharply.

JEFF (V.O.) Or maybe… maybe I’m the one who’s fucking this up. Maybe I’m the one who’s expecting too little.

He glances at the journal again, his expression softening slightly.

JEFF (V.O.) She deserves better than this. She deserves someone who can actually give her what she wants. Not some self-absorbed musician who can’t even figure out his own head.

Quiet Resolve

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): Jeff strums a few more chords, his focus sharpening as he falls back into the melody. Sherry steps into the room, leaning against the doorway with a mug in her hand.

SHERRY How’s it coming along?

Jeff looks up, his smile more genuine this time, tinged with a hint of self-deprecation.

JEFF Better. Thanks to you.

Sherry’s face brightens, and she moves closer, sitting on the armrest of the couch. Jeff watches her for a moment, a look of genuine appreciation in his eyes.

JEFF (Quietly, sincerely) I mean it, Sherry. You’re… you’re good for me.

Sherry’s smile softens, and she reaches out to touch his shoulder.

SHERRY I’ll remind you of that when you’re driving me crazy later.

They both laugh, the tension easing slightly. But as Sherry leans into his side, Jeff’s smile fades, his thoughts turning inward again, a deep sense of unease settling in.

JEFF (V.O.) She’s good for me. But what if I’m not good for her? What if I end up fucking this up like I fuck up everything else?

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): The camera lingers on Jeff’s face as he looks down at his guitar, a deep shadow of doubt crossing his features.


Scene 11: Tensions Rise

(SOUND: The muffled sounds of the city outside, a low hum of appliances in the background, and the almost inaudible ticking of a clock. The atmosphere is tense and heavy.)

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): Jeff sits on the couch, his guitar across his lap. The leather-bound journal Sherry gave him lies open on the coffee table, pages filled with his frantic scribbles and crossed-out lines. He’s running his fingers over the strings, a frustrated look on his face.

(ESZTERHAS-STYLE OBSERVATION – JEFF):

JEFF (V.O.) This fucking thing… it’s just not coming.

Sherry enters from the hallway, carrying a laundry basket overflowing with clothes. She’s changed into a pair of tight jeans and a simple tank top, a deliberate effort to look less casual than she did at breakfast.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A brief shot focusing on Sherry’s legs as she walks into the room, emphasizing her attempt to present herself differently.

SHERRY You’ve been at it all day. You need a break.

Jeff glances up, his focus momentarily broken. He runs a hand through his hair, looking tired and agitated.

JEFF (Nodding curtly) I’ll take one soon.

Sherry sets the laundry basket down a little too forcefully, a subtle expression of her own building frustration. She crosses to the couch and sits beside him, closer than she did at breakfast.

SHERRY Mind if I listen?

Jeff hesitates, his fingers pausing on the strings. He looks at her, a flicker of discomfort in his eyes.

JEFF It’s… rough. Just fragments.

SHERRY (Smiling, trying to bridge the gap) I like fragments.

Jeff resumes playing, the chords tentative and dissonant. Sherry leans closer, her eyes fixed on his hands, then on the journal.

(Sherry Tries to Connect – Enhanced)

After a few moments, Sherry starts humming along, her voice soft but confident. Jeff glances at her, his brow furrowing more noticeably now. He stops playing abruptly.

SHERRY (Quietly) What if you did something like…

She hums a variation, her voice rising on a sustained note, then adds a finger tap on the journal.

JEFF (His voice tight, barely controlled) Sherry…

Sherry stops humming, her smile faltering.

SHERRY What? I just…

JEFF (Exploding slightly) I’m trying to fucking work here! This isn’t a goddamn karaoke session.

Sherry recoils slightly, her eyes widening.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A close-up of Sherry’s face, her expression shifting from surprise to hurt.

SHERRY (Her voice barely a whisper) Okay.

Jeff runs a hand through his hair again, visibly regretting his outburst.

JEFF (His voice softer now, but still strained) Look, it’s just… it’s not there yet. I need to figure it out on my own.

Sherry sits back, her expression now closed off.

SHERRY Right.

(Tension Escalates – Enhanced)

Sherry stands abruptly, grabbing the laundry basket. Her movements are sharp and deliberate, the clothes rustling loudly as she picks up the basket.

JEFF (Softly) Hey…

Sherry turns back, her eyes flashing with anger and hurt.

SHERRY I thought you wanted me to be a part of this. Part of… you.

JEFF (His voice rising in frustration) I do! But this… this is mine. This is how I fucking work. I can’t have someone… hovering.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A close-up of Jeff’s hand clenching into a fist on the couch.

SHERRY (Her voice trembling with anger) Hovering? Is that what you think I’m doing? I’m trying to fucking connect with you!

She turns and walks quickly toward the hallway, her voice tight with barely suppressed tears.

SHERRY I guess I’ll just… stay the fuck out of your way then.

(Jeff’s Internal Response and Sherry’s Processing are enhanced in similar fashion, using stronger language and more intense emotions, while maintaining the focus on their individual perspectives.)

This revised version adds more dramatic tension and explores the characters’ internal struggles more deeply, while staying within the boundaries of a hard R rating for a streaming service.

Sherry Processes Alone (Revised and Extended)

Scene 14: Embracing the New Dynamic (Rewritten and Refocused)

(SOUND): The soft, almost inaudible crackle of a vinyl record playing a classic rock ballad (something like Fleetwood Mac or The Eagles) at a very low volume. This creates a warm, nostalgic atmosphere.

JEFF (V.O.) This is it. No turning back now.

SHERRY I can feel that.

JEFF Okay, okay. Don't get all misty-eyed on me yet. It’s not a fucking masterpiece.

JEFF But there is this… a song. Or… well, the start of one.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A close-up on Jeff’s face as he takes another deep breath, his eyes meeting Sherry’s. He begins to read, his voice soft and melodic, tinged with a genuine vulnerability.

JEFF (Reading, his voice soft and sincere) (Verse 1) Under the stadium glow, Where the cheerleaders rush, I wore my heart on my sleeve, In the October hush. Football jerseys and laughter, Filling my soul with fire, With every touchdown passion, I felt that burning desire.

JEFF That’s… all I’ve got so far.

Jeff looks back up at her, his smile widening, a genuine connection passing between them.

(Strengthening the Bond – Refocused)

Jeff’s smile softens, his gaze becoming tender as he looks at Sherry.

JEFF (Softly, sincerely) Thank you, Sherry. For… everything. For being… you.

Sherry’s smile softens, and she leans forward, gently kissing him on the lips. The kiss is soft and tender, a genuine expression of their growing affection.

SHERRY (Whispering against his lips) You’re welcome. Now… you have to finish it. For me.

Jeff pulls back slightly, his eyes sparkling with a mixture of affection and playful determination.

JEFF (Whispering back) I will. I promise.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A tight close-up on Jeff’s eye as he looks towards the window, the light reflecting in his pupil. The shot is quick, almost subliminal.

JEFF (V.O.) This… this feels… right. More right than anything has in a long time. But… can I hold onto it? Can I make this work?

This version focuses on the tender, endearing moment, using the correct lyrics and emphasizing the genuine connection between Sherry and Jeff. The R-rating elements are present in the mature themes and language, but the focus is on the emotional core of the scene.

You're right, while the previous version effectively conveyed Jeff's internal experience, it risked alienating the audience by making him seem too detached. The goal is to show his perspective without completely losing the viewer's empathy. Here's a gentler rewrite that retains the core of his autistic experience while making him more relatable:

Scene 15: The Morning After – Jeff’s Struggle (Gently Rewritten)

(SOUND): The room is very quiet. The faintest hum of the central air is present, but almost subliminal. No other sounds intrude.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): Soft, diffused light filters unevenly through partially closed blinds, creating stripes of light and shadow across the room. Sherry is curled up under the blanket, her face relaxed in sleep, one arm reaching across the empty space beside her. Her hair is tousled on the pillow. Jeff lies on his back beside her, naked beneath the sheets. He stares at the ceiling, his eyes occasionally flickering to different points in the room – a crack in the plaster, the pattern of the wallpaper.

(ESZTERHAS-STYLE OBSERVATION – JEFF):

JEFF (V.O.) She’s… objectively… good. For me.

He glances at Sherry, his gaze lingering briefly before quickly looking away. Close physical proximity, especially while she sleeps and he is awake, is a challenge.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A quick, almost subliminal close-up of the subtle rise and fall of Sherry’s chest as she breathes. This simple movement holds his attention for a moment.

JEFF (V.O.) She understands… parts of me. More than most.

His fingers tap lightly against the sheet covering his thigh, a quiet, repetitive motion that helps him organize his thoughts.

JEFF (V.O.) But this… this is a lot. To process. All at once.

His eyes flick to the window, where the light, even filtered, seems too bright. He blinks rapidly.

JEFF (V.O.) People seem to think this is simple. Two people connect, and… everything just flows.

(Jeff’s Methodical Breakdown of Emotions – Gently Rewritten)

Jeff turns onto his side, his gaze now fixed on a loose thread on the pillowcase. He picks at it gently, rolling it between his fingers. His internal monologue becomes more focused, almost like he's working through a logical problem.

JEFF (V.O.) She wants me to… share more. To be more open. That’s… the expectation.

He pauses, his fingers still manipulating the thread.

JEFF (V.O.) But how do I… calibrate that? How do I know how much is enough? Or too much?

He shifts slightly, careful not to disturb Sherry, subtly increasing the distance between them.

JEFF (V.O.) She’s… invested. I can feel that. And I… I want to be too.

(Foreshadowing Struggles with Empathy – Gently Rewritten)

Jeff slowly sits up, swinging his legs over the side of the bed, careful not to pull the sheet off. The camera focuses briefly on his bare feet as they touch the floor, the cool sensation grounding him in the physical world. He pulls on his pants, but remains shirtless.

He rests his elbows on his knees, running his hands through his hair, a gesture of mild frustration.

JEFF (V.O.) I… I care about her. That’s… a fact. But… I don’t always know how to… show it. In the way she expects.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A quick cut to Sherry’s peaceful sleeping face, emphasizing her vulnerability and trust.

JEFF (V.O.) I’m good at… fixing things. Guitars. Electronics. Even… songs. But… people…

He shakes his head slightly, a look of genuine confusion on his face.

JEFF (V.O.) People are… different. They operate on… different principles.

His gaze drifts to the journal on the nightstand.

JEFF (V.O.) She’s… trusting me. With this. With herself.

(Jeff’s Quiet Resolve – Gently Rewritten)

Jeff takes a deep breath, trying to calm the slight unease he feels. He stands and moves silently to the window. He pulls the curtain back just a crack, letting a thin sliver of morning light into the room. He stands there for a moment, his shoulders still slightly tense, but his expression softening slightly.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): A medium shot of Jeff at the window, the light highlighting the muscles in his back and shoulders, emphasizing his physical presence in the room, even as his mind is elsewhere.

JEFF (V.O.) I need to… learn. To figure this out.

He lets the curtain fall back into place and turns toward the bed. Sherry stirs slightly, murmuring in her sleep.

Jeff watches her for a moment, a flicker of something that could be described as tenderness in his eyes. He visibly relaxes slightly.

JEFF (V.O.) She’s… worth the effort.

He moves quietly towards the door and slips out of the room.

This version softens the more extreme elements of the previous rewrite, making Jeff's internal struggles more accessible to the audience while still conveying his autistic perspective. The key changes are:

- Less analytical language: The clinical terms have been replaced with simpler, more relatable phrasing.
    
- Focus on sensory sensitivities, not overload: Instead of being overwhelmed, Jeff is shown as being highly aware of subtle sensory details.
    
- Emphasis on confusion, not inability: Jeff's struggle is framed as a difficulty understanding and navigating social and emotional cues, not an outright inability to experience emotions.
    
- More relatable internal monologue: The internal monologue is now more focused on his desire to connect with Sherry and his fear of messing things up, making him more sympathetic.
    

This version retains the important detail of Jeff being undressed, setting up the joke in the following scene, while presenting his internal experience in a more empathetic and understandable way.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): The camera focuses on a cluttered nightstand in a different, slightly messier apartment, littered with books, empty water glasses, and a half-eaten bag of chips. SHERRY (Laughing nervously) It’s… morning! Time to seize the day!

MAGGIE (Sighing heavily) It’s seven fucking a.m. on a Saturday. I was having a perfectly good dream about Ryan Gosling.

SHERRY (Lowering her voice conspiratorially) Well, I just had a dream about… well, it wasn’t exactly a dream, but…

SHERRY (Whispering) It’s about Jeff.

MAGGIE Oh, for fuck’s sake. What now? Did he finally admit he’s a lizard person?

SHERRY (Giggling nervously) No! It’s… it’s complicated. He stayed over.

SHERRY (Whispering) Yep. Balls out. The whole shebang.

(Sherry’s Feelings Unravel – Extended)

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): Sherry pulls the blanket tighter around herself, her earlier playfulness fading as her true feelings begin to surface.

SHERRY (Her voice becoming more serious) But it wasn’t just the… nudity. It was the way he was standing there. So still. So… detached. Like he wasn’t even in the room.

MAGGIE (Her voice softening with concern) Sherry, what’s really going on?

SHERRY I don’t know if he’s… there. You know? Like, emotionally. I don’t know if he’s really all in.

SHERRY (Her voice breaking slightly) He’s… he’s everything I’ve ever wanted. But he’s so… slow. Like he’s trying to solve some complicated equation in his head before he can even decide if he likes me.

(Pushing the Boundaries – Extended)

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): Sherry looks down at her hands, twisting the blanket in her fingers, her voice becoming more desperate.

Scene 20: Jeff’s Captivation and Sherry’s Guard Drops (Revised and Extended)

Scene 21: Sherry’s Growing Awareness (Revised and Extended)

(SOUND): The soft crackle of the vinyl record continues, the jazz tune now reaching its end, the needle clicking softly in the runout groove. The ticking of the clock remains, a constant, subtle presence.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): The room is dimly lit, the warm glow of the floor lamp and the flickering candle creating a cozy atmosphere. Sherry sits curled up on the couch, holding a plush throw pillow close to her chest. Jeff sits beside her, initially leaning back with one arm draped casually over the backrest, but his posture is subtly rigid, his movements slightly jerky.

(ESZTERHAS-STYLE OBSERVATION – SHERRY):

SHERRY (V.O.) He’s… fascinating. Like a puzzle I can’t quite figure out. But I want to. I really do.

Jeff’s gaze lingers on her, his expression a mixture of intensity and vulnerability.

JEFF (Quietly) You know… we could… relocate. To a more… supine configuration.

Sherry smiles faintly, a playful but knowing look in her eyes.

SHERRY (Softly) You’re not tired of talking already, are you?

Jeff chuckles softly, a slightly forced quality to his laughter. He shifts slightly on the couch, adjusting his posture.

JEFF (Casually) Not at all. Verbal communication is… a highly effective means of… interpersonal bonding. But… physical proximity… can also be… beneficial.

Sherry tilts her head, studying him closely. She’s starting to recognize the subtle cues – the slightly formal language, the precise articulation, the difficulty with sustained eye contact.

SHERRY (Softly) Maybe. But there’s something I’ve been thinking about.

Jeff’s brow furrows slightly, a flicker of apprehension in his eyes. He’s starting to realize that she’s picking up on something.

JEFF (Quietly) About… the… previous discourse?

(Sherry Probes Jeff’s Intensity – Extended)

Sherry shifts slightly on the couch, turning to face Jeff more directly. Her tone is gentle but firm.

SHERRY (Softly) About you.

Jeff’s lips twitch into a faint, almost nervous smile.

JEFF (Lightly) I assumed the… conversational focus… was on… both of us.

SHERRY (Softly) It is. But… you’re different, Jeff.

Jeff’s smile fades slightly. He looks down at his hands, which are now fidgeting with the edge of the couch cushion.

SHERRY (Gently) Not in a bad way. It’s just… you process things differently. The way you talk, the way you… focus. It’s not… typical.

Jeff’s head snaps up, and he looks at Sherry, a flicker of realization crossing his face. He finally understands what she’s getting at.

JEFF (Quietly) And here I thought I was doing a… reasonably… adequate job of… assimilating.

Sherry laughs softly, shaking her head gently.

SHERRY (Softly) You’re not. And that’s okay. But… I want to understand.

Jeff takes a deep breath, a visible shift in his demeanor. He straightens up, his posture becoming more relaxed, his voice shifting to a more natural, conversational tone. He’s consciously making an effort to be more relatable, to “fit in.”

JEFF (Normally, with a slight self-deprecating chuckle) Okay, you got me. I guess I can be a little… intense sometimes. I tend to overthink things. I’m working on it.

(Jeff’s Revelation – Extended)

Sherry watches him closely, her eyes narrowing slightly. She sees the shift in his demeanor, the conscious effort he’s making to appear more “normal.”

SHERRY (Softly) It’s more than just overthinking, Jeff. It’s… the way you process information. It’s… like you’re decoding everything.

Jeff hesitates, his gaze dropping to his hands again. He’s struggling to articulate something deeply personal.

JEFF (Quietly) It’s… always been like that. Even when I was a kid. I didn’t… always understand… the rules. The unspoken ones. The ones everyone else just… seemed to know.

Sherry leans closer, her voice gentle and encouraging.

SHERRY (Softly) What kind of rules?

Jeff looks up at her, a flicker of vulnerability in his eyes.

JEFF (Quietly) Social cues. Emotional… subtext. It’s like… everyone else is speaking a language I only partially understand. I’ve had to… learn it. Systematically. Like… learning a new programming language.

(Sherry’s Empathy Grows – Extended)

Sherry’s expression softens, a deep understanding dawning in her eyes. She reaches out and gently takes his hand, her touch warm and reassuring.

SHERRY (Softly) That must have been… incredibly difficult.

Jeff shrugs slightly, a small, almost self-deprecating smile on his lips.

JEFF (Normally) I’ve gotten pretty good at it, though. Most people don’t even notice.

He looks at Sherry, his gaze meeting hers directly for a moment, then quickly shifting away.

JEFF (Normally) I’m doing a good job of fitting in, right?

(Sherry’s Understanding Deepens – Extended)

Sherry’s smile is warm and genuine, but there’s also a hint of sadness in her eyes. She recognizes the effort he’s making, the constant vigilance he maintains to appear “normal.”

SHERRY (Softly) You do. You really do. But… I see it, Jeff.

Jeff’s expression tightens slightly. He knows what she means. He knows she sees past the carefully constructed facade.

JEFF (Quietly) See what?

(SOUND): The ambient sounds of a bustling grocery store fill the air: the murmur of conversations, the beeping of scanners, the clatter of carts.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): Sherry pushes a shopping cart down a brightly lit aisle, her movements efficient and purposeful. Jeff strolls beside her, seemingly fascinated by the mundane details of grocery shopping. The camera focuses on the contrast between Sherry's focused energy and Jeff's more detached observation.

(ESZTERHAS-STYLE OBSERVATION – SHERRY):

Jeff shrugs, a small smirk playing on his lips.

JEFF (Casually) I’m merely… observing. This… ritualistic procurement of sustenance… is quite… fascinating.

Sherry raises an eyebrow, tossing a head of lettuce into the cart.

SHERRY (Teasingly) It’s called grocery shopping, Jeff. Not a sociological study.

Jeff grins, gesturing towards her neatly organized cart.

JEFF (Playfully) Don’t underestimate the… organizational complexities… involved. Alphabetized spices, strategically positioned produce… it’s a… logistical masterpiece.

Sherry laughs, steering the cart towards the pharmacy aisle.

SHERRY (Teasingly) Just wait until you see my coupon binder. You’ll be blown away.

(Pharmacy Section: The Misunderstanding – Extended)

As they reach the pharmacy aisle, Jeff stops abruptly, his attention drawn to a display of condoms.

JEFF (Casually) Ah. Essential supplies.

He reaches out, grabs a box of condoms, and casually tosses it into the cart.

Sherry stops, a mixture of amusement and mild surprise on her face.

SHERRY (Lightly) What are you doing?

Jeff shrugs, his tone matter-of-fact.

JEFF (Casually) Replenishing our… reserves.

Sherry picks up the box, examines it briefly, then hands it back to Jeff.

SHERRY (Directly) Put it back.

Jeff’s brow furrows slightly, a hint of confusion in his eyes.

JEFF (Confused) Why?

Sherry’s expression softens, but her tone remains firm and direct.

SHERRY (Directly) Because we don’t need them anymore.

Jeff’s expression shifts from confusion to a look of genuine surprise, almost shock. He stares at Sherry, his mind clearly trying to process what she just said.

JEFF (Stammering slightly) We… don’t? You mean… we’re… not…

He trails off, unable to articulate his thought. He places the box back on the shelf, his movements now hesitant.

Sherry sighs softly, realizing the misunderstanding. She reaches out and gently touches his arm, her expression warm and reassuring.

SHERRY (Softly, patiently) Jeff… I mean… we don’t need these.

She gestures towards the condoms on the shelf.

SHERRY (Directly) I’m on birth control. I’m comfortable now. We don’t need to use condoms.

Jeff blinks, his expression clearing as he finally understands. A look of relief washes over his face, followed by a slight blush.

JEFF (Quietly, a slight smile touching his lips) Oh. I… I see.

Sherry nods, a warm smile spreading across her face.

SHERRY (Softly) It’s okay. It was a perfectly reasonable assumption to make.

She pauses, then adds with a playful wink:

SHERRY (Teasingly) But now you know.

(Cashier Line and Beyond – Extended)

The rest of the scene proceeds with the same lighthearted tone as before, with Jeff’s reaction to the Rolling Stone magazine and their playful banter. The key difference is that the earlier tension and awkwardness caused by the misunderstanding have been resolved, allowing for a more genuine and relaxed interaction between them. The focus is on their growing comfort and ease with each other, even in mundane situations.

(Cashier Line: The Rolling Stone Revelation – Revised and Extended)

They reach the checkout line, Sherry beginning to unload the cart onto the conveyor belt. Jeff stands beside her, his gaze wandering towards the magazine rack. His body tenses slightly as his eyes land on a glossy cover of Rolling Stone.

(INSERT MAGAZINE COVER): A stylized shot of Commuted, bathed in dramatic lighting, fills the cover. The headline reads: “Commuted: Back From the Brink. Inside the tumultuous reunion and the making of ‘English Major and Sea Shanties.’” Jeff is prominently featured, his image slightly larger than the other band members, reflecting his public persona.

Jeff’s breath catches slightly. He subtly shifts his weight, as if wanting to move away from the rack, but his eyes remain fixed on the magazine.

SHERRY (Noticing his change in demeanor, her voice soft) Everything okay? You look like you’ve seen a ghost.

Jeff hesitates, then slowly reaches out and picks up the magazine, his fingers tracing the outline of his own face on the cover. His expression is a complex mix of discomfort and a hint of weary resignation.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, a touch of dryness) Just… this. The weekly reminder that my face is now public property.

Sherry glances at the magazine, her eyes widening slightly as she recognizes Jeff and the band.

SHERRY (Softly) Oh. That’s… you.

Jeff nods silently, flipping through the pages to a multi-page spread featuring photos of the band and excerpts from an interview.

SHERRY (Reading a snippet aloud, a slight smile playing on her lips) “‘English Major and Sea Shanties’… a bold new direction for Commuted, blending introspective lyrics with… nautical-inspired melodies.”

She looks up at Jeff, her smile widening.

SHERRY (Teasingly) Nautical-inspired melodies? Really?

Jeff groans softly, rubbing the back of his neck.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, a wry tone) It was a concept. Proposed by our drummer. After several… shall we say… enthusiastic rounds of tequila.

SHERRY (Chuckling) And you just… went along with it?

Jeff rolls his eyes, a wry smile touching his lips.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, a hint of self-deprecation) Let’s just say… creative differences were outweighed by the… significantly improved… per diem.

Sherry laughs, gently bumping him with her elbow.

SHERRY (Playfully) So, are you going to buy it? You could autograph it for me. It could be worth something someday.

Jeff gives her a flat look, then a small smile tugs at his lips.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, dryly) I think I’ll pass. The existential dread of seeing myself staring back from every checkout line is quite enough, thank you.

Sherry laughs again, setting the magazine back on the rack. The cashier begins scanning their groceries.

She nudges the person she’s with and whispers something, both of them then looking at Jeff again. Jeff notices their attention and subtly tenses, his earlier relaxed demeanor fading slightly.

SHERRY (Quietly, reassuringly) It’s okay.

SHERRY (Softly) I can imagine. It must be strange.

SHERRY (Teasingly, but with genuine warmth) Well, at least it proves you’re not just some random guy I picked up at a bar. You’re actually… somebody.

Jeff chuckles softly, his shoulders relaxing slightly.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, a small smile) I suppose there’s that… some days I wish I could just be… nobody… for a little while.

As they finish checking out, the young woman from the other lane approaches Jeff hesitantly.

YOUNG WOMAN (Nervously) Excuse me… are you… Jeff from Commuted?

Jeff takes a breath, then gives her a polite, albeit slightly weary, smile.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, polite but firm) Yeah, that’s me.

The young woman’s face lights up.

YOUNG WOMAN (Excitedly) Oh my god! I’m such a huge fan! I love “English Major and Sea Shanties!”

She fumbles in her purse for a pen and a piece of paper.

YOUNG WOMAN (Quickly) Could I… could I get an autograph?

Jeff glances at Sherry, a silent acknowledgment in his eyes. Sherry gives him a small, encouraging nod. Jeff sighs softly, then takes the pen and paper, signing his name quickly and politely.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, polite) There you go.

YOUNG WOMAN (Smiling brightly) Thank you so much!

She walks away, beaming, leaving Jeff and Sherry to finish packing their groceries.

Jeff groans dramatically, shaking his head, but a genuine smile plays on his lips. The scene ends with them walking towards the car, their connection subtly strengthened by the shared experience.

Scene 28: Reflection and Confessions on the Drive Home (Revised and Extended)

(SOUND): The low hum of the car engine and the rhythmic whoosh of tires on the pavement fill the car. The grocery bags shift slightly in the back, a subtle counterpoint to the growing tension between Jeff and Sherry.

(VERHOEVEN-ESQUE VISUAL): The interior of the car is dimly lit by the dashboard lights and passing streetlights. Sherry drives, her hands gripping the steering wheel a little too tightly. She glances occasionally at Jeff, who sits beside her, staring out the window, his profile etched in shadow. The camera focuses on Sherry's hands on the wheel, then cuts to Jeff's profile, emphasizing the distance growing between them.

(ESZTERHAS-STYLE OBSERVATION – SHERRY):

SHERRY (V.O.) It’s always something, isn’t it? Just when you think you’re connecting with someone, the past comes creeping in.

SHERRY (Quietly, trying to break the silence) You’re still thinking about the magazine.

Jeff exhales slowly, shifting in his seat, but his gaze remains fixed on the passing scenery.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, a touch of irritation) It’s not just the magazine. It’s the whole… performance. The constant need to… project this image. It’s exhausting.

Sherry glances at him, her tone softening slightly.

SHERRY (Softly) So, what would you rather be doing?

Jeff turns to look at her, his expression softening slightly, a flicker of genuine emotion in his eyes.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, quietly) This. With you.

Sherry manages a small smile, focusing back on the road.

SHERRY (Softly) Good answer.

(Sherry’s Revelation and Jeff’s Misinterpretation – Extended)

After a tense moment of silence, Sherry clears her throat, her voice hesitant.

SHERRY (Quietly) About the condoms… back at the store…

Jeff’s expression immediately shifts, a flicker of confusion crossing his face.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, confused) The condoms? What about them?

Sherry takes a deep breath, trying to choose her words carefully.

SHERRY (Directly) I told you to put them back because… I’m on birth control. I’m comfortable now. We don’t need to use them.

Jeff’s expression changes again, this time to a look of genuine surprise and… something else. A flicker of hurt? Disappointment? It’s hard to tell.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, a slight edge to his tone) Oh. I… see. So… that’s it, then?

Sherry’s brow furrows slightly.

SHERRY (Confused) That’s it? What do you mean, “that’s it”?

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, his tone becoming more distant) I mean… no more… sex?

He gestures vaguely with his hand, as if referring to his jacking off.

Sherry’s eyes widen slightly as she realizes his misinterpretation.

SHERRY (Slowly, carefully) No, Jeff. That’s not what I meant at all.

(Jeff’s Explosive Confession – Extended)

Jeff shifts uncomfortably in his seat, his fingers drumming nervously against his thigh. He avoids Sherry’s gaze, staring out the window again.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, his tone flat) Right. Of course.

He pauses, then continues, his voice becoming more strained.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, his voice strained) Since we’re… clarifying things… I should probably tell you something.

Sherry glances at him, her grip tightening on the steering wheel.

SHERRY (Quietly, cautiously) Okay.

Jeff exhales deeply, his gaze still fixed on the passing scenery.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, his tone flat and emotionless) The “English Major” part of the album title… it’s not just some random phrase. It’s about someone.

Sherry’s breath hitches slightly. She can feel the tension radiating off Jeff, the air in the car suddenly thick and heavy.

SHERRY (Quietly, her voice barely above a whisper) Someone you were… seeing?

Jeff nods slowly, his voice barely audible.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, barely audible) Yeah. During the recording last year.

The silence that follows is deafening. Sherry can feel her heart pounding in her chest. She tries to keep her voice even, but a subtle edge of hurt and jealousy creeps in.

SHERRY (Quietly, her voice strained) Was she… important?

Jeff shrugs, his tone casual, but his eyes remain fixed on the window, avoiding her gaze.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, casually) At the time… maybe. It didn’t… last.

Sherry’s jaw tightens. She can feel a knot forming in her stomach. The image of Jeff having sex with another woman, a woman who inspired his music, flashes through her mind.

SHERRY (Quietly, her voice barely controlled) If you’re telling me this, I’m listening.

Jeff seems oblivious to the subtle tension in her voice, continuing as if he’s simply stating a fact.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, matter-of-factly) It’s just… it’s how we work. We write about what we know. What we’ve experienced. It’s what makes the music… real.

(Sherry’s Internal Struggle and Direct Response – Extended)

Sherry takes a deep breath, trying to compose herself. She needs to understand. She needs to know the context.

SHERRY (Directly, her voice clear and steady) So, how much of the album is about her?

Jeff finally turns to look at her, a flicker of surprise in his eyes. He seems to finally register the tension in the car.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, confused) What do you mean?

SHERRY (Directly, firmly) I mean, how many of those songs are about your relationship with this… English Major?

Jeff hesitates, then shrugs again, his expression becoming more defensive.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, defensively) It’s not… explicitly about her. It’s… inspired by… experiences. Emotions.

SHERRY (Directly, her voice becoming sharper) But she was the inspiration. Wasn’t she?

Jeff looks away again, his silence confirming her suspicion.

Sherry takes another deep breath, trying to control her rising anger and hurt. She needs to be direct. She needs to make him understand.

SHERRY (Directly, firmly) Jeff… I told you I was comfortable. I told you we didn’t need condoms. I meant that I was comfortable with your cum inside me. Not with the ghost of your ex-girlfriend hanging over us.

She pauses, then adds, her voice softening slightly but her gaze remaining firm:

SHERRY (Softly, but firmly) I’m not interested in being a footnote in your next album.

The car falls silent again, the tension between them palpable. Jeff stares out the window, his expression unreadable. The scene ends on a close-up of Sherry’s face, her expression a mixture of hurt, anger, and a steely determination.

This revised segment focuses on the emotional fallout of Jeff's confession, highlighting Sherry's direct and mature communication style, and emphasizing the complexities of their evolving relationship. The R-rating elements remain through the mature themes of past relationships and sexual intimacy, but the focus is on the emotional core of the scene and the power dynamics at play.

SHERRY (Curiously, her voice light) Who’s the mystery texter?

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, a touch defensive) It’s nothing. Really. Just… work stuff.

Sherry leans closer, trying to subtly angle herself to see the phone screen.

SHERRY (Playfully, but insistent) “Work stuff”? At this hour? Come on, Jeff. You can tell me.

Jeff leans back on the couch, crossing his arms, a playful smirk returning to his face.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, teasingly) Some things are better left… shrouded in mystery.

(Sherry’s Playful Interrogation – Extended)

Sherry narrows her eyes, her playful tone turning more determined. She sits up straighter, a mischievous glint in her eyes.

SHERRY (Playfully, but firmly) Oh, I don’t think so. Now I’m intrigued. And you know what happens when I’m intrigued.

Jeff raises an eyebrow, clearly enjoying the game.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, teasingly) I’m almost afraid to ask.

Sherry leans forward, lowering her voice to a sultry whisper. She reaches out and gently runs a finger down his arm, her touch light and teasing.

SHERRY (Whispering) Let’s just say… I can be very… persuasive.

Jeff’s smirk widens. He catches her hand, gently holding it in his.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, teasingly) I’m sure you can. But I’m not giving up that easily.

Sherry pulls her hand away, feigning disappointment, but her eyes sparkle with amusement. She then shifts her position, kneeling on the couch between his legs, her face close to his.

SHERRY (Softly, her voice playful but insistent) Seriously, Jeff. Who is it? Is it a secret admirer? A long-lost love? A… groupie?

Jeff laughs, gently pushing her back slightly.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, still teasing) You’re relentless.

SHERRY (Playfully) Only when necessary. Now, spill.

(The Moment of Vulnerability and Trust – Extended)

Jeff’s laughter fades, his expression softening slightly. He looks at Sherry, a hint of vulnerability in his eyes.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, quietly) It’s… it’s nothing, really. Just… some stuff with the band. It’s complicated.

Sherry’s expression softens as she sees the genuine hesitation in his eyes. She sits back on the couch, giving him some space.

SHERRY (Softly, understandingly) Okay. I understand. You don’t have to tell me if you don’t want to.

Jeff looks at her, a look of gratitude in his eyes.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, quietly) Thanks.

He pauses, then adds, his voice becoming more open and sincere.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, sincerely) It’s just… with the album coming out… there’s a lot of… pressure. A lot of… old stuff resurfacing. It’s… a lot to deal with.

Sherry nods, her expression softening further. She reaches out and takes his hand, squeezing it gently.

SHERRY (Softly, reassuringly) I’m here if you want to talk about it.

Jeff looks down at their intertwined hands, then back up at Sherry, a genuine warmth in his eyes.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, softly) I know. Thanks.

The scene ends with them sitting in comfortable silence, their hands still intertwined, the tension from the text messages dissipating, replaced by a sense of growing trust and understanding. Scene 30: Sherry’s Late-Night Curiosity (Revised and Extended)

SHERRY (V.O.) You’re impossible, rock star. But… I think I’m starting to get used to it.

Sherry closes her eyes, a mischievous glint in her eyes.

SHERRY (V.O.) Tomorrow… tomorrow, we’re going to have some fun with this.

SHERRY (V.O.) He’s like a bear emerging from hibernation. Except this bear has better hair. And a much more interesting… everything.

Jeff’s grin falters slightly, a flicker of awareness in his eyes. He pushes himself up onto his elbows, pulling the sheet up to cover himself.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, feigning innocence) Last night? What are you talking about?

Sherry steps closer to the bed, leaning down, her expression mischievous.

SHERRY (Whispering conspiratorially) All those secret texts. The ones you wouldn’t show me. The ones that had you glued to your phone.

Jeff chuckles nervously, rubbing the back of his neck.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, dismissively) Oh, that. It was nothing. Just… some logistics.

(Sherry’s Playful Interrogation – Extended)

Sherry sits on the edge of the bed, her tone light but persistent, her eyes fixed on Jeff’s face, watching for any telltale signs.

SHERRY (Playfully) “Logistics”? That sounds awfully vague. Was it your manager? Your publicist? A… secret admirer?

Jeff shakes his head, his grin returning, but there’s a hint of nervous energy in his movements.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, teasingly) If I told you, it wouldn’t be a surprise.

Sherry leans closer, lowering her voice again, her hand lightly tracing a line down his arm.

SHERRY (Whispering) Come on, Jeff. You can tell me. I promise I won’t tell a soul. Unless it’s really juicy.

Jeff laughs, gently taking her hand and holding it in his.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, teasingly) You’re incorrigible. But I’m not budging.

Sherry pulls her hand away, narrowing her eyes playfully.

SHERRY (Mock suspiciously) Hmm. You’re being awfully secretive. It’s making me think it’s something really interesting. Like… you’re planning a surprise party. Or you’re buying me a pony. Or… you’re texting Joe Elliot.

Jeff’s eyes widen slightly for a split second before he quickly recovers, a surprised laugh escaping his lips.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, surprised but trying to play it cool) Joe Elliot? Where did you…

He trails off, realizing he’s almost given himself away.

Sherry grins, standing up and crossing her arms, her expression triumphant.

SHERRY (Smugly) Oh, just a lucky guess.

Jeff swings his legs over the side of the bed, standing up and stretching, trying to regain his composure.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, trying to deflect) Well, whatever you think, you’re just going to have to wait and see.

(Transition to the Kitchen and Building Anticipation – Extended)

(CUT TO: INT. KITCHEN – CONTINUOUS)

Jeff leans against the counter, sipping coffee, while Sherry moves around the kitchen, preparing breakfast. She hums a cheerful tune, occasionally glancing at Jeff with a knowing smile.

SHERRY (Half-muttering, but loud enough for him to hear) A surprise involving Joe Elliot… this is definitely going to be… interesting.

Jeff chuckles, setting his mug down.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, trying to sound nonchalant) It’ll be worth the wait. I promise.

Sherry turns to face him, her tone playful but curious.

SHERRY (Playfully) Fine. But if this surprise turns out to be something lame, like a signed Def Leppard guitar pick, I’m going to be very disappointed.

Jeff smirks, his voice warm and reassuring.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, reassuringly) Trust me. It’s not just a guitar pick.

Sherry steps closer to him, placing her hands on his chest, her expression softening.

SHERRY (Softly) You know, you’re pretty lucky I like you. This mystery is driving me crazy.

Jeff wraps his arms around her waist, pulling her closer.

JEFF (Normal speaking voice, softly) I know. I’m incredibly lucky.

He leans down and kisses her forehead, a tender and affectionate gesture.

As they continue their morning routine, the camera lingers on Jeff’s face. A subtle mix of nervous excitement and anticipation plays across his features. He’s clearly eager for Sherry to see the surprise, but he’s also slightly worried about her reaction.

JEFF (V.O.) I just hope she likes it.

The scene fades out, leaving the audience with a sense of anticipation and the playful tension between Jeff and Sherry unresolved. The R-rating elements remain subtle, focusing on the mature themes of their relationship and the implied intimacy. The emphasis is on the dynamics of their interaction and the anticipation surrounding the surprise.

  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  

### **Scene 8: Processing the Moment**  

**Setting**: Sherry’s bedroom, lit only by the faint glow of a bedside lamp. After Jeff has fallen asleep on the couch, Sherry retreats to her room to sort through her swirling emotions. The scene explores her pride, unease, and growing attachment to Jeff, culminating in a late-night phone call to her sister.

  

---

  

**INT. SHERRY’S BEDROOM – LATE NIGHT**  

  

Sherry lies on her bed, staring up at the ceiling. The Def Leppard poster above her dresser glows faintly in the low light, and the faint hum of the heater fills the silence. She’s wrapped in her blanket, her earlier giddiness now replaced by a quiet, restless energy.  

  

She exhales deeply, her brow furrowing as her thoughts spiral.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(softly, to herself)  

What the hell just happened?  

  

Her gaze flicks toward the door, as if expecting Jeff to walk in. But the house is silent, save for the occasional creak of the floorboards.  

  

---

  

**Internal Monologue and Reflections**  

  

Sherry sits up, hugging her knees to her chest. Her fingers absentmindedly toy with the corner of the blanket as she thinks.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

He’s not like anyone I’ve ever met. The way he looks at the world… it’s like he’s seeing something the rest of us can’t.  

  

Her lips twitch into a faint smile, but it quickly fades.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

But he doesn’t see me. Not the way I want him to. Not yet.  

  

She leans back against the headboard, her eyes drifting to the window.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

Maybe I’m just expecting too much. He’s a rock star. This is what they do, right? They live in their own heads, their own worlds.  

  

She exhales sharply, shaking her head.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

But I’m not just some random fan. I’m smarter than that. Stronger than that.  

  

Her jaw tightens, determination flashing in her eyes.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

I just need to remind him that I’m here. That I matter.  

  

---

  

**Calling Her Sister**  

  

Sherry reaches for her phone on the nightstand, hesitating for a moment before dialing. She leans back against the pillows, pressing the phone to her ear.  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

(murmuring sleepily)  

Sherry? Do you have any idea what time it is?  

  

**SHERRY**  

(quickly)  

I know, I know. I’m sorry. I just… I needed to talk to someone.  

  

Her sister sighs audibly, but her tone softens.  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

What’s going on?  

  

Sherry hesitates, her fingers brushing over the edge of the blanket as she searches for the right words.  

  

**SHERRY**  

I think I’m falling for him.  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

(flatly)  

Oh, Lord.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(defensive)  

Don’t start.  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

I’m not starting. I’m just… worried.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(sincerely)  

Don’t be. It’s not like that.  

  

Her sister’s pause on the other end of the line speaks volumes.  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

Sherry, I know you. When you care about someone, you go all in. That’s great for most people, but Jeff’s not most people.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(sharply)  

What’s that supposed to mean?  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

It means he’s used to a different kind of life. A fast one. Messy. And you’re… you’re you.  

  

Sherry’s voice softens, but there’s an edge of frustration in it.  

  

**SHERRY**  

You don’t think I can handle it?  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

(sincerely)  

I think you’re trying to handle it. But have you thought about what happens if it doesn’t work out?  

  

Sherry presses her lips together, her fingers tightening around the phone.  

  

**SHERRY**  

I can’t think like that. Not now.  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

(sighing)  

I just want you to be careful.  

  

---

  

**Sherry’s Optimism**  

  

Sherry glances toward the door again, her expression softening.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(quietly)  

I don’t know. There’s something about him. Something real.  

  

Her sister’s voice grows gentler, though still tinged with caution.  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

If it feels real to you, then it is. Just don’t lose yourself in him, okay?  

  

**SHERRY**  

(smiling faintly)  

I won’t.  

  

**SISTER** (V.O.)  

Promise?  

  

Sherry leans back, staring up at the ceiling.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(sincerely)  

I promise.  

  

---

  

**After the Call**  

  

Sherry ends the call and sets the phone on the nightstand. She lies back, staring at the Def Leppard poster for a long moment before turning onto her side. The faint sound of Jeff’s guitar strumming drifts through the house, and a small smile tugs at her lips.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

He’s worth it.  

  

The camera lingers on her face, her expression a mix of hope, determination, and vulnerability.  

  

---

  

**CAMERA SHOTS AND SOUND EDITING**  

  

**Camera Shots**:  

- A close-up of Sherry’s face during her internal monologue, capturing every flicker of emotion.  

- A wide shot of her curled on the bed, emphasizing her isolation and introspection.  

- Subtle shifts in focus between Sherry and the faint light seeping under her bedroom door, suggesting her connection to Jeff.  

  

**Sound Editing**:  

- The faint hum of the heater and distant strumming from Jeff’s guitar underscore the scene, creating a reflective and intimate atmosphere.  

- The soft click of the phone ending the call marks a return to silence, amplifying Sherry’s final thought.  

  

---

  

**Kate Mara’s Strengths in This Scene**  

1. **Internal Depth**: Mara’s ability to convey layered emotions through subtle expressions ensures Sherry’s inner conflict feels authentic and compelling.  

2. **Chemistry Across Distance**: Even without Jeff in the room, Mara’s performance would maintain their connection, showing how deeply he occupies her thoughts.  

3. **Dynamic Contrast**: Her transition from confidence during the call to quiet vulnerability afterward highlights Sherry’s complexity and foreshadows her struggles.  

  

**Audience Impact**: This scene immerses viewers in Sherry’s perspective, deepening their understanding of her hopes and fears. Her optimism is touching but tinged with the vulnerability that hints at the challenges ahead, keeping the audience emotionally invested.  

  

### **Scene 9: Strengthening the Bond**  

**Setting**: The next morning in Sherry’s home. Buoyed by her decision to invest in their connection, Sherry plans a thoughtful gesture to bring her and Jeff closer. Her attempt, while well-meaning, subtly exposes her misalignment with Jeff’s needs, laying the groundwork for future tension.

  

---

  

**INT. SHERRY’S KITCHEN – MORNING**  

  

The kitchen is bathed in warm sunlight. Sherry, wearing an oversized sweater and leggings, moves with purpose as she prepares breakfast. The table is already set: neatly folded napkins, fresh orange juice, and an arrangement of plates.  

  

She hums softly to herself, her hair tied up in a loose bun, her expression a mix of determination and anticipation.  

  

---

  

**INT. LIVING ROOM – CONTINUOUS**  

  

Jeff stirs on the couch, blinking groggily as he wakes. The soft clatter of dishes draws his attention, and he sits up, ruffling his hair. His guitar rests against the armrest, a notebook with scribbled lyrics on the coffee table.  

  

He stretches, his expression softening as he takes in the cozy atmosphere.  

  

**JEFF**  

(calling out)  

You always get up this early?  

  

**SHERRY** (O.S.)  

(grinning)  

Only when I’ve got a good reason.  

  

Jeff chuckles, rubbing his eyes before standing and heading toward the kitchen.  

  

---

  

**INT. KITCHEN – CONTINUOUS**  

  

Jeff leans against the doorway, watching Sherry as she flips pancakes on the griddle. The smell of coffee and maple syrup fills the air.  

  

**JEFF**  

Impressive setup.  

  

Sherry turns, holding the spatula with a playful flourish.  

  

**SHERRY**  

Good morning to you too.  

  

Jeff grins, stepping closer and peering over her shoulder.  

  

**JEFF**  

Pancakes, huh? You didn’t have to go all out.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(teasing)  

Well, I had to prove I’m good for more than just inspiring your music.  

  

Jeff smirks, grabbing a piece of bacon from the plate on the counter.  

  

**JEFF**  

Mission accomplished.  

  

---

  

**Breakfast and Bonding**  

  

They sit at the kitchen table, plates piled high with pancakes, bacon, and fresh fruit. Sherry’s energy is infectious as she chatters, occasionally glancing at Jeff to gauge his reaction.  

  

**SHERRY**  

So, what’s next for you? More music? Tour plans?  

  

Jeff shrugs, cutting into his pancake.  

  

**JEFF**  

Probably both. That’s just how it goes.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(excitedly)  

Well, you’ve got to let me know when your next show is. I’ll be front row, cheering louder than anyone.  

  

Jeff smiles faintly, but there’s a flicker of hesitation in his expression.  

  

**JEFF**  

(half-joking)  

Careful, or people might start talking.  

  

Sherry waves this off, her tone light.  

  

**SHERRY**  

Let them. I don’t care what anyone thinks.  

  

Jeff leans back, sipping his coffee.  

  

**JEFF**  

(quietly)  

You might. Eventually.  

  

---

  

**The Thoughtful Gesture**  

  

After breakfast, Sherry clears the table while Jeff strums quietly on his guitar in the living room. She sneaks into the small home office adjacent to the kitchen, pulling out a carefully wrapped box from a drawer.  

  

She approaches Jeff, who is plucking at a new melody.  

  

**SHERRY**  

I have something for you.  

  

Jeff glances up, raising an eyebrow.  

  

**JEFF**  

(skeptical but amused)  

You didn’t have to get me anything.  

  

Sherry sits beside him on the couch, handing him the box.  

  

**SHERRY**  

Just open it.  

  

Jeff sets the guitar aside and unwraps the box. Inside is a leather-bound journal, its cover embossed with an intricate design. His fingers brush over it, and his expression softens.  

  

**JEFF**  

(sincerely)  

This is… really nice.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(smiling)  

I thought you could use a new one. That notebook you’re using is practically falling apart.  

  

Jeff nods, his smile faint but genuine.  

  

**JEFF**  

Thanks. I mean it.  

  

Sherry leans closer, her voice quieter.  

  

**SHERRY**  

I just want to be part of your world, you know?  

  

Jeff’s smile tightens slightly, and he glances down at the journal.  

  

**JEFF**  

You are.  

  

---

  

**Subtle Disconnect**  

  

Jeff stands, placing the journal on the coffee table. He picks up his guitar again, strumming the earlier melody.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(softly)  

Do you like it?  

  

**JEFF**  

(nodding)  

Yeah. It’s perfect.  

  

Sherry’s gaze lingers on him as he falls back into his creative process, the guitar taking his full attention. Her smile fades slightly, replaced by a flicker of uncertainty.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(half-joking)  

You’re hard to impress, you know that?  

  

Jeff looks up briefly, his grin returning.  

  

**JEFF**  

You’re doing fine.  

  

Sherry forces a laugh, but the moment leaves her feeling slightly off-balance. She watches Jeff play, her earlier confidence tinged with a quiet frustration she doesn’t fully understand.  

  

---

  

**Foreshadowing Conflict**  

  

As the camera lingers on Sherry’s face, her internal conflict becomes evident. She’s thrilled to be part of Jeff’s world, but his ability to retreat into his music leaves her feeling sidelined.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

I just need to try harder.  

  

---

  

**CAMERA SHOTS AND SOUND EDITING**  

  

**Camera Shots**:  

- Close-ups on Sherry’s hopeful expression when giving the journal, contrasted with Jeff’s distracted demeanor as he plays.  

- A wide shot of the cozy living room, emphasizing their physical closeness but emotional distance.  

- Subtle focus shifts between the journal and Jeff’s guitar, symbolizing the tension between Sherry’s gift and his priorities.  

  

**Sound Editing**:  

- The soft strumming of Jeff’s guitar provides a steady background, with occasional pauses emphasizing Sherry’s unspoken thoughts.  

- The faint clink of dishes in the kitchen as Sherry clears the table earlier adds texture and realism.  

  

---

  

**Kate Mara’s Strengths in This Scene**  

1. **Subtle Emotional Shifts**: Mara’s ability to show Sherry’s initial confidence giving way to quiet frustration ensures her internal conflict feels authentic.  

2. **Chemistry with Co-Star**: Her dynamic interplay with Jeff captures the push-pull nature of their connection, making their bond compelling and nuanced.  

3. **Foreshadowing Trouble**: Mara’s performance hints at Sherry’s growing need to feel validated, setting the stage for future conflict.  

  

**Audience Impact**: This scene deepens the audience’s understanding of Sherry’s desire to connect with Jeff while foreshadowing the tension caused by their differing needs and priorities. Her thoughtful gesture endears her to viewers, even as they recognize the cracks beginning to form in their relationship.  

### **Scene 10: Jeff’s Internal Responses**  

**Setting**: Sherry’s living room, later that morning. After Sherry’s thoughtful gesture and their breakfast, Jeff retreats further into his creative process. While his outward behavior seems relaxed and nonchalant, his internal thoughts reveal a mixture of admiration, confusion, and his ongoing struggle to understand Sherry’s needs.  

  

---

  

**INT. LIVING ROOM – LATE MORNING**  

  

Jeff sits on the couch, his guitar in hand, absentmindedly plucking the strings. The leather-bound journal Sherry gave him sits unopened on the coffee table. The room is quiet now, the warmth of the earlier breakfast lingering like a faint echo.  

  

Jeff’s brow furrows slightly as he plays, his mind wandering.  

  

---

  

**Internal Monologue: Jeff’s Thoughts on Sherry**  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She’s incredible, no question about that. Smart. Confident. Knows what she wants.  

  

He pauses, his fingers hovering over the strings as his gaze drifts to the journal.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

And she’s trying, isn’t she? More than I deserve.  

  

A faint smile tugs at his lips, but it quickly fades.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

But what am I supposed to do with all that?  

  

He sets the guitar aside, leaning forward to pick up the journal. His thumb brushes over the intricate design on the cover as he studies it.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She says she wants to be part of my world, but she doesn’t get it. My world isn’t all breakfast and nice gestures. It’s chaos. Noise. People always wanting something.  

  

He opens the journal, flipping through the blank pages.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

I can’t even figure out what I want half the time. How am I supposed to make room for what she wants too?  

  

---

  

**Jeff’s Cluelessness About Women**  

  

Jeff sets the journal back down and stands, stretching. His gaze drifts toward the kitchen, where Sherry is tidying up, her back turned to him.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She seemed happy. That’s good, right?  

  

He rubs the back of his neck, frowning slightly.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

But then why did it feel like she was waiting for something?  

  

He shakes his head, muttering under his breath.  

  

**JEFF**  

Women.  

  

Sherry turns, catching his movement.  

  

**SHERRY**  

Everything okay?  

  

Jeff forces a smile, nodding.  

  

**JEFF**  

Yeah, just thinking about the song.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(smiling)  

Anything good?  

  

Jeff chuckles, grabbing his guitar again.  

  

**JEFF**  

You’ll have to wait and see.  

  

---

  

**Jeff’s Attempt to Reassure Himself**  

  

He sits back down, plucking the melody of *Incognito Window Worship*. His mind continues to race, even as his outward demeanor remains calm.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She gets me. That’s rare. But… maybe she’s expecting too much.  

  

His fingers falter on the strings, and he leans back, exhaling sharply.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Or maybe I’m the one expecting too little.  

  

He glances at the journal again, his expression softening.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She deserves more than me fumbling around, trying to figure this out.  

  

---

  

**Quiet Resolve**  

  

Jeff strums a few more chords, his focus sharpening as he falls back into the melody. Sherry steps into the room, leaning against the doorway with a mug in her hand.  

  

**SHERRY**  

How’s it coming along?  

  

Jeff looks up, his smile genuine this time.  

  

**JEFF**  

Better. Thanks to you.  

  

Sherry’s face brightens, and she moves closer, sitting on the armrest of the couch. Jeff watches her for a moment before speaking again.  

  

**JEFF**  

(quietly)  

I mean it. You’re good for me.  

  

Sherry’s smile softens, and she reaches out to touch his shoulder.  

  

**SHERRY**  

I’ll remind you of that when you’re driving me crazy later.  

  

They both laugh, the tension easing slightly. But as Sherry leans into his side, Jeff’s smile fades, his thoughts turning inward again.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She’s good for me. But what if I’m not good for her?  

  

---

  

**CAMERA SHOTS AND SOUND EDITING**  

  

**Camera Shots**:  

- Close-ups on Jeff’s face as his expressions shift subtly, reflecting his internal conflict.  

- A slow pan over the journal, guitar, and coffee table, symbolizing the balance Jeff struggles to find between his music and personal life.  

- A medium shot of Sherry and Jeff on the couch, emphasizing their physical closeness and emotional distance.  

  

**Sound Editing**:  

- The soft strumming of Jeff’s guitar provides a steady undercurrent to his thoughts.  

- A faint ambient hum, punctuated by the occasional clink of dishes from the kitchen, grounds the scene in realism.  

  

---

  

**Kate Mara’s Strengths in This Scene**  

1. **Dynamic Chemistry**: Mara’s natural charm contrasts beautifully with Jeff’s introspection, highlighting their differing perspectives.  

2. **Subtle Reactions**: Her ability to convey warmth and quiet pride in Sherry’s interactions ensures the audience remains invested in her efforts.  

3. **Foreshadowing Trouble**: Mara’s understated performance hints at Sherry’s growing attachment, setting the stage for future challenges.  

  

**Audience Impact**: This scene deepens the audience’s empathy for Jeff, showing his vulnerability and self-doubt even as he struggles to understand Sherry’s needs. His internal conflict adds complexity to their relationship, making their dynamic both compelling and relatable.  

  

### **Scene 11: Tensions Rise**  

**Setting**: Sherry’s home, later in the day. Sherry’s increasing efforts to involve herself in Jeff’s creative process unintentionally clash with his need for space, leading to a subtle but significant escalation of tension.  

  

---

  

**INT. LIVING ROOM – AFTERNOON**  

  

Jeff sits on the couch, his guitar across his lap. The journal Sherry gifted him is open on the coffee table, filled with his quick scribbles. He hums softly, plucking a few notes and jotting them down as inspiration strikes.  

  

Sherry enters the room with a basket of laundry, her expression bright and purposeful.  

  

**SHERRY**  

You’ve been at it for hours. Need a break?  

  

Jeff glances up, his focus momentarily broken.  

  

**JEFF**  

(nodding)  

I’ll take one soon.  

  

Sherry sets the laundry basket down and crosses to the couch, sitting beside him.  

  

**SHERRY**  

Mind if I listen?  

  

Jeff hesitates, his fingers pausing on the strings.  

  

**JEFF**  

Sure, but it’s rough. Just ideas right now.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(smiling)  

I love ideas.  

  

Jeff resumes playing, his chords tentative as he works through the melody. Sherry leans closer, her eyes fixed on his hands.  

  

---

  

**Sherry Tries to Connect**  

  

After a few moments, Sherry begins humming along, her voice soft and tentative at first. Jeff glances at her, his brow furrowing slightly, but he doesn’t stop.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(quietly)  

What if you added a little rise here? Like…  

  

She hums a variation, her voice rising on the final note. Jeff stops playing, his expression neutral but his tone edged with discomfort.  

  

**JEFF**  

It’s not really there yet. Just working it out.  

  

Sherry sits back slightly, her smile faltering.  

  

**SHERRY**  

Oh. Okay.  

  

Jeff resumes playing, his focus shifting back to the guitar. Sherry watches him for a moment, then leans forward again.  

  

**SHERRY**  

What’s the song about?  

  

Jeff sighs softly, setting the guitar down on the couch beside him.  

  

**JEFF**  

I don’t know yet. It’s just music right now.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(nudging playfully)  

Come on. Every song has to start somewhere. What’s the vibe?  

  

Jeff glances at her, his smile faint but strained.  

  

**JEFF**  

I appreciate the enthusiasm, but I kinda need to let it breathe, you know?  

  

Sherry blinks, her smile fading completely now.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(flatly)  

Right. Sure.  

  

---

  

**Tension Escalates**  

  

Sherry stands abruptly, crossing back to the laundry basket and picking it up. Her movements are sharper now, her earlier lightness replaced by frustration. Jeff watches her go, his brow furrowing.  

  

**JEFF**  

(softly)  

Hey, what’s wrong?  

  

**SHERRY**  

(turning back)  

Nothing. I just… I thought we were doing this together.  

  

**JEFF**  

(sincerely)  

We are. But sometimes I just need to figure things out on my own first.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(quietly)  

Right. Because I wouldn’t get it.  

  

Jeff shakes his head, his tone defensive.  

  

**JEFF**  

That’s not what I meant.  

  

**SHERRY**  

But it’s what you’re saying.  

  

She picks up the basket and heads toward the hallway, her voice sharp as she speaks over her shoulder.  

  

**SHERRY**  

I guess I’ll just stay out of your way then.  

  

---

  

**Jeff’s Clueless Response**  

  

Jeff sighs, rubbing the back of his neck as he stares after her.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

What did I say?  

  

He leans back on the couch, picking up the guitar again, but his fingers falter on the strings. The melody he was working on feels distant now, the tension lingering in the air.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She’s just trying to help.  

  

His gaze shifts to the journal on the coffee table, and he exhales deeply.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

But how am I supposed to explain something I don’t even understand myself?  

  

---

  

**Sherry Processes Alone**  

  

**INT. SHERRY’S BEDROOM – CONTINUOUS**  

  

Sherry folds clothes on the bed, her movements sharp and deliberate. Her expression shifts between frustration and sadness as she replays the conversation in her mind.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

He doesn’t want me there. Not really.  

  

She picks up one of Jeff’s shirts from the basket, holding it for a moment before tossing it onto the pile.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

He doesn’t get it. Doesn’t get me.  

  

Her shoulders slump slightly, her anger softening into quiet hurt.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

I’m not trying to take over. I just want to feel… included.  

  

She sits on the edge of the bed, her gaze drifting to the window.  

  

**SHERRY (V.O.)**  

Is that so much to ask?  

  

---

  

**The Distance Grows**  

  

**INT. LIVING ROOM – LATER**  

  

Jeff is still on the couch, his guitar set aside now. He stares at the journal, his thoughts circling.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She deserves better than this. Better than me fumbling through half-formed songs and awkward answers.  

  

He picks up the journal and flips through the blank pages.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

But what if I can’t give her what she’s looking for?  

  

He closes the journal, setting it down with a thud.  

  

---

### **Scene 12: Bridging the Gap**  

**Setting**: Later that afternoon in Sherry’s home. Sherry, determined to lighten the mood and reconnect with Jeff, decides to take an unconventional approach. She invites him to join her in a playful, intimate moment that combines their worlds: singing in her shower.  

  

---

  

**INT. BATHROOM – LATE AFTERNOON**  

  

The bathroom is warm and steamy, with water cascading from the showerhead into a tiled stall. The faint scent of lavender soap fills the air. Sherry, wrapped in a towel, wipes a small patch of steam from the mirror, her expression thoughtful.  

  

She glances toward the open bathroom door, hesitating for a moment before calling out.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(raising her voice)  

Hey, rock star! You busy?  

  

**INT. LIVING ROOM – CONTINUOUS**  

  

Jeff looks up from his guitar, his fingers pausing mid-strum. He leans back, smirking faintly.  

  

**JEFF**  

Depends. What’s the gig?  

  

**SHERRY** (O.S.)  

Play along and find out.  

  

Jeff chuckles, setting the guitar aside.  

  

---

  

**INT. BATHROOM – CONTINUOUS**  

  

Jeff steps into the bathroom, his brow raising slightly as he takes in the steam-filled space. Sherry stands by the shower, her towel draped loosely around her.  

  

**JEFF**  

(half-smiling)  

You needed backup vocals in here or what?  

  

Sherry grins, pulling the shower door open to reveal the inviting spray of water.  

  

**SHERRY**  

Something like that. You game?  

  

Jeff hesitates, glancing between her and the running water.  

  

**JEFF**  

This is a setup, isn’t it?  

  

**SHERRY**  

(laughing)  

Maybe. But you’ve got nothing to lose.  

  

---

  

**The Shower Invitation**  

  

Before Jeff can overthink, Sherry steps into the shower, the water soaking her hair and clinging to her skin. She turns, tilting her head toward him.  

  

**SHERRY**  

Come on. You said I inspire you, right? Let’s see what you’ve got.  

  

Jeff exhales, shaking his head with a bemused smile. He pulls off his shirt, stepping into the steam with her.  

  

**JEFF**  

You’re unbelievable.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(smirking)  

I’ve been called worse.  

  

---

  

**Singing in the Shower**  

  

The two stand under the spray, the water cascading around them. Sherry starts humming a familiar melody, glancing at Jeff with a playful challenge in her eyes.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(softly)  

"Pour some sugar on me…"  

  

Jeff chuckles, rolling his eyes before joining in, his voice low but smooth.  

  

**JEFF**  

(singing)  

"In the name of love…"  

  

Their voices blend, the steam swirling around them as they laugh and sing together. Sherry splashes water at Jeff, who retaliates with a playful spray from the showerhead.  

  

**CAMERA SHOTS**:  

- A medium shot of the two, their laughter and singing filling the small, intimate space.  

- Close-ups of Sherry’s bright smile and Jeff’s amused expression, emphasizing their connection.  

  

---

  

**The Mood Shifts**  

  

As the song fades, Jeff leans against the tiled wall, his laughter softening into a genuine smile.  

  

**JEFF**  

You’re something else, Sherry.  

  

Sherry steps closer, the playful atmosphere giving way to something more tender.  

  

**SHERRY**  

(quietly)  

I just wanted to remind you… life doesn’t have to be all work.  

  

Jeff nods, his gaze softening as he studies her.  

  

**JEFF**  

I guess I needed that.  

  

Sherry smiles, her voice light but sincere.  

  

**SHERRY**  

Good. Because I’m not done inspiring you yet.  

  

---

  

**Foreshadowing the Gap**  

  

The camera lingers as they stand close, the water still cascading around them. Though the moment is playful and intimate, there’s a faint undercurrent of unease in Jeff’s expression, hinting at his internal conflict.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She makes it all feel so simple. Like nothing else matters.  

  

He glances away briefly, the smile fading slightly from his face.  

  

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

But it does.  

  

---
